xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi><mi>n</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbb{R}^n</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">\mathbb{R}^n</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, we use </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> Cl(n, 0) </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span If the set requires a different signature (e.g., Minkowski space for spacetime applications), we could use </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">(</span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> Cl(p, q) </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">)</span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, where </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>q</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>n</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">p + q = n</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">p + q = n</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, and the quadratic form is:
</span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5 r-13awgt0 r-18u37iz r-1777fci r-1vx7f1k r-tux3g4 r-13qz1uu"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mi>Q</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo fence="true">{</mo><mtable rowspacing="0.36em" columnalign="left left" columnspacing="1em"><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mn>1</mn></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mtext>for&nbsp;</mtext><mi>i</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mo>…</mo><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>p</mi><mo separator="true">,</mo></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mtext>for&nbsp;</mtext><mi>i</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>p</mi><mo>+</mo><mn>1</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mo>…</mo><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>p</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>q</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">.</mi></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr></mtable></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Q(e_i) = \begin{cases} 
1 &amp; \text{for } i = 1, \dots, p, \\
-1 &amp; \text{for } i = p+1, \dots, p+q.
\end{cases}</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex_block" style="display: none;">Q(e_i) = \begin{cases} <br>1 &amp; \text{for } i = 1, \dots, p, \\<br>-1 &amp; \text{for } i = p+1, \dots, p+q.<br>\end{cases}</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">
For simplicity, let’s assume </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> (Euclidean signature) unless the "harmonic" aspect suggests a specific signature (e.g., spacetime algebra </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 multivectors </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>S</mi><mo>=</mo><mo 0)</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> is a multivector:
</span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5 r-13awgt0 r-18u37iz r-1777fci r-1vx7f1k r-tux3g4 r-13qz1uu"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><munderover><mo>∑</mo><mrow><mi>j</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><mi>n</mi></munderover><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo><mi>j</mi></msub><mo separator="true">,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">M_i = \sum_{j=0}^n \langle M_i \rangle_j,</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex_block" style="display: none;">M_i = \sum_{j=0}^n \langle M_i \rangle_j,</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">
and </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\langle M_i \rangle_j</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">\langle M_i \rangle_j</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> is the grade-</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">(</span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> j </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">)</span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> component of </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">M_i</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">M_i</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">. The set </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo multivectors of varying grades, and we want to construct a single multivector </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo (pseudoscalar). The term "harmonic" suggests a partitioning or organization of multivectors inspired by harmonic analysis or symmetry, with the partitioning sequence (2, 3, 5, ...) indicating the number of subsets for each harmonic.</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>S</mi><mo>=</mo><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo separator="true">,</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo separator="true">,</mo><mo>…</mo><mo separator="true">,</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>k</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S = \{M_1, M_2, \dots, M_k\}</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">S = \{M_1, M_2, \dots, M_k\}</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, where each </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><msubsup><mo>∑</mo><mrow><mi>j</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><mi>n</mi></msubsup><mo \rangle_j</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">M_i = \sum_{j=0}^n \langle M_i \rangle_j</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, is to be partitioned based on these harmonics. The "top and bottom" likely refer to a representative multivector </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">(</span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> M </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">)</span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> that captures the extremal grades (e.g., scalar for "bottom" and highest grade for "top") of the set or its partitions.</span></span></span></span><hr style="margin-top: 3em; This suggests a hierarchical or iterative structure where each harmonic level organizes the multivectors into a prime number of subsets, potentially based on their algebraic properties (e.g., grade, magnitude, or geometric role).</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 part).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">The term "harmonic" and the prime number sequence suggest a connection to harmonic analysis or number theory. In Clifford algebra, we can interpret harmonics as:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>∈</mo><mi>S</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">M_i \in S</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">M_i \in S</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> (Euclidean signature for simplicity, unless otherwise specified) represents a concept or term. These embeddings encode semantic or structural information, similar to word embeddings in natural language processing (NLP), but within the algebraic structure of a Clifford algebra.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Harmonic Partitioning</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: The first harmonic partitions </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">(</span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> S </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">)</span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> into 2 subsets, the second into 3, the third into 5, and so on, following the prime numbers (2, 3, 5, 7, ...). This suggests a hierarchical clustering or decomposition of the embeddings based on their algebraic or semantic properties.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Top and Bottom</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: The representative multivector </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">(</span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> M </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">)</span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> for the set (or each harmonic) combines the scalar component (grade 0, "bottom") and the highest-grade component (e.g., bivector or pseudoscalar, "top") to summarize the set’s properties.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; \overline{M_i} M_j \rangle_0</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> (where multivectors with similar embeddings.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">∥</mi><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mi mathvariant="normal">∥</mi><mo>=</mo><msqrt><mrow><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>⋅</mo><mover accent="true"><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo stretchy="true">‾</mo></mover></mrow></msqrt></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\|M_i\| = \sqrt{M_i \cdot \overline{M_i}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Harmonic Interpretation</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">The harmonic partitioning (2, 3, 5, ...) resembles a semantic or algebraic decomposition:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Semantic Clustering</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Each harmonic groups concepts by increasing granularity (e.g., animals vs. objects in the first harmonic, then finer categories like "furry animals," "non-furry animals," "furniture").</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Algebraic Structure</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span graded structure encoding relationships (e.g., bivectors for pairwise interactions).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 encodes complex relationships or orientations.</span></span></span></li></ul><hr style="margin-top: 3em; margin-bottom: 3em; border-color: rgb(62, 65, 68);"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">M_i = \sum_{k=0}^n \langle M_i \rangle_k</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">M_i = \sum_{k=0}^n \langle M_i \rangle_k</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> encodes semantic features, with scalar (grade 0) and higher-grade components (e.g., vectors, bivectors, up to the pseudoscalar).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Bipartite Graph Analogy</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: For the first harmonic (</span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">h=1</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">h=1</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, 2 subsets), the set </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>S</mi><mo>=</mo><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo separator="true">,</mo><mo>…</mo><mo separator="true">,</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>k</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S = \{M_1, \dots, M_k\}</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">S = \{M_1, \dots, M_k\}</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> of multivector embeddings is naturally partitioned into two subsets, </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msubsup><mi>S</mi><mn>1</mn><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S_1^{(1)}</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msubsup><mi>S</mi><mn>2</mn><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S_2^{(1)}</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: In a bipartite graph, vertices are divided into two disjoint sets such that connections (edges) exist only between sets, not within them. This suggests the concepts have a natural dichotomy (e.g., animals vs. objects, abstract vs. concrete).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Harmonic Partitioning</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">)</span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> into 3, 5, 7, ... subsets (following prime numbers), possibly refining the bipartite structure or using a new criterion (e.g., semantic or algebraic properties).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 multivector </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi>M</mi><mrow><mo </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo style="display: none;">S_1^{(1)}</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> and </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msubsup><mi>S</mi><mn>2</mn><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msubsup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">S_2^{(1)}</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">S_2^{(1)}</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, reflecting a natural bipartite structure. This could be based on:</span></span></span><ul style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0.75em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Semantic Dichotomy</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Concepts naturally fall into two groups (e.g., "cat," "dog" vs. "table," "chair").</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Algebraic Properties</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Use the inner product </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>⋅</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mover accent="true"><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo stretchy="true">‾</mo></mover><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo><mn>0</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">M_i \cdot M_j = \langle \overline{M_i} M_j \rangle_0</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">M_i \cdot M_j = \langle \overline{M_i} M_j \rangle_0</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> (where </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mover accent="true"><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo stretchy="true">‾</mo></mover></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\overline{M_i}</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">\overline{M_i}</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> is the reverse) to measure similarity. Cluster multivectors into two groups such that </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>⋅</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">M_i \cdot M_j</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">M_i \cdot M_j</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> is high within groups and low between groups, mimicking bipartite graph edges.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Grade-Based</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Separate multivectors with dominant lower grades (e.g., scalars, vectors) from those with higher grades (e.g., bivectors, pseudoscalars).</span></span></span></li></ul></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Example: For concepts like "cat," "dog," "table," "chair," the bipartite split might group animals (</span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msubsup><mi>S</mi><mn>1</mn><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo r-poiln3">).</span></span></span></li></ul></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span by:</span></span></span><ul style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0.75em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span where each harmonic increases the number of semantic or structural categories.</span></span></span></li></ul></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span construct:</span></span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5 r-13awgt0 r-18u37iz r-1777fci r-1vx7f1k r-tux3g4 r-13qz1uu"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi>M</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></msup><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>α</mi><mi>h</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>S</mi></msub><msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo><mn>0</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>β</mi><mi>h</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>S</mi></msub><msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo><mi>m</mi></msub><mo separator="true">,</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">M^{(h)} = \alpha_h \langle M_S \rangle_0 + \beta_h \langle M_S \rangle_m,</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex_block" style="display: none;">M^{(h)} = \alpha_h \langle M_S \rangle_0 + \beta_h \langle M_S \rangle_m,</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">where:</span></span></span><ul style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0.75em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>S</mi></msub><msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo><mn>0</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mi>k</mi></mfrac><msubsup><mo>∑</mo><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mi>k</mi></msubsup><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msub><mi>M</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo><mn>0</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\langle M_S \rangle_0 = \frac{1}{k} ### User

<span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1x3r274 r-p1pxzi"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">ok great and then we can embed the idea of 2 and 3 itself into this schema. so we can embed the numerical representation of the system itself in the system</span></span></span></span>

### Grok AI

<span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">This is a fascinating extension of the harmonic Clifford algebra framework! You’re proposing to embed the numerical concepts of the partitioning scheme itself (i.e., the numbers 2, 3, 5, etc., representing the number of subsets in each harmonic) into the same Clifford algebra used for the concept embeddings. This creates a self-referential system where the structure of the harmonics (the prime numbers defining the partitions) is encoded as multivectors alongside the concepts/terms. The representative multivector continues to capture the "top and bottom" (scalar and highest-grade components), and the first harmonic leverages a bipartite graph-like structure. Below, I provide a concise and tailored approach to incorporate this self-referential embedding within the harmonic Clifford algebra framework.</span></span></span></span><hr style="margin-top: 3em; margin-bottom: 3em; border-color: rgb(62, 65, 68);"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-adyw6z r-135wba7 r-b88u0q" style="display: block; margin-top: 1.5em; margin-bottom: Cl(n, 0) </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo Simple but limited, as it ignores higher grades.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Vector Embedding</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Map </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>h</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">p_h</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">p_h</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> to a vector, e.g., </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>N</mi><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>h</mi></msub></msub><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>h</mi></msub><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">N_{p_h} = p_h e_1</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">N_{p_h} = p_h e_1</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, using a fixed basis element. ### Grok AI

Please provide details to refine the solution!</span></span></span></span>
